221H 114V 1807952X 6C Mem:1 Exits:D> d
The Clerics Guild
Young clerics and priests once travelled long distances to come here to
study and worship. An elaborate altar was once the centerpiece of this
chamber, but now it is gone and no one has visited or worshipped here in
ages. The marble floor is cracked and uneven in several places, but still
this room has a feeling of divinity and importance.
Witz the Male Hill Dwarf is standing here. (flying) (invisible)
. . . has a tough exterior.
Eligarf the Male Human is standing here. (flying) (invisible)
. . . has a tough exterior.

221H 114V 1807952X 6C Mem:1 Exits:S> s

Loath flies in from the north.
Witz flies in from the north.
Within the Broken Temple
This large, now-empty chamber once served as the entryway into the
Tarsis temple. The floor, once a polished, shiny marble, is dull and
cracked, having lost it's sheen long ago. There is a chamber to the north
that served as the clerics guild, and the exit to the temple lies to the
east.
Witz the Male Hill Dwarf is standing here. (flying) (invisible)
. . . has a tough exterior.
Loath the Male Wild Elf is standing here. (flying) (invisible)
. . . has a tough exterior.
Eligarf the Male Human is standing here. (flying) (invisible)
. . . is outlined with a dim aura.

Western Road
This road runs east-west, from the Tarsis fountain towards the
wastelands. A small road leads north from here, past the old Tarsis temple
and towards the park. Immediately to the south is a row of broken
buildings, most of them empty shells or heaps of rubble.

Near the Tarsis Wastelands
The broken road continues westward, towards the Tarsis Wastelands which
was once known for the vagrants and criminals that occupied the area. Now
it, like the rest of the city, is barren and desolate. A road branches off
to the south, leading towards the cities inn, while the main road leads
eastward, towards the city square.

The Tarsis Wastelands
Once, these Wastelands served as a walking ground for muggers,
prostitutes, thieves and the like, but now it is dead and barren. The
remains of a large ship that was grounded here can be seen to the south,
but it had collapsed onto itself a long time ago, destroying whatever might
have been in it.

221H 104V 1807952X 6C Mem:1 Exits:NES> s
Eligarf flies in from the north.
Loath flies in from the north.
Witz flies in from the north.
The Tarsis Dump
A forsaken desert surrounds you, swallows you whole with its forceful
gales that hurl grains of sand deep into your skin. It is as if the wind is
penetrating your bones. Scattered pieces of brick and stone have been
discarded here in the dump. Where once a steady stream of horse-drawn cart
would carry the refuse of tarsis to this forsaken landfill, nothing stirs.
There is little here that is still useful, but the ancient bones of what
you can assume were vagrants lie amidst the trash, with the hopes of their
once peaceful lives covered with filth.
Witz the Male Hill Dwarf is standing here. (flying) (invisible)
. . . has a tough exterior.
Loath the Male Wild Elf is standing here. (flying) (invisible)
. . . has a tough exterior.

Forgotten Stables
The eastern half of this huge building has collapsed onto itself,
leaving half of the stables buried and unusable. Most of the horse stalls
have been destroyed or fallen to ruin. This chamber has not seen a horse
for several ages, but the smells normally associated with horses still
lingers here.

221H 94V 1807952X 6C Mem:1 Exits:NESW> Eligarf flies in from the north.
Loath flies in from the north.
Witz flies in from the north.
A Shattered Gate
The southern gates of Tarsis were once heavily fortified, reinforced
steel, unlike their wooden counterparts at the north and east gates. These
gates were made specifically to keep something out, and to make sure that
it stayed out, especially since Icewall was to the south of this city
before the Gods took it away. The heavy fortifications and magical
enchantments on this gate are probably the only reason the gates still rest
on their massive hinges, although those hinges have long since rusted
solid.
Witz the Male Hill Dwarf is standing here. (flying) (invisible)
. . . has a tough exterior.
Loath the Male Wild Elf is standing here. (flying) (invisible)
. . . has a tough exterior.
Eligarf the Male Human is standing here. (flying) (invisible)
. . . has a tough exterior.

Before the Library
Two large wooden double doors in the southern wall once opened to
scholars seeking the knowledge and wisdom that was housed within the Great
Tarsis Library. Now only a single, beaten door remains, barely hanging from
its rusted hinges, threatening to fall and shatter itself on the stone
floor. The wall to the north is a crumbling testament to the power of time
and neglect: what was once relied upon to protect the city from invaders is
little more than a mound of stones that a small child could surmount.

Before the Courthouse
The building to the south once served as the city hall and courthouse
for Tarsis. Even now, in its dilapidated state, the building still has an

The Ruined Market
Broken stone tiles crunch under your feet; the massive stone tiles that
once endured the footfalls of men and horses alike lie shattered and broken
here. The surrounding buildings are in the same condition: several have
missing walls and roofs while others have entirely collapsed onto
themselves.

The Tarsis Dump
A forsaken desert surrounds you, swallows you whole with its forceful
gales that hurl grains of sand deep into your skin. It is as if the wind is
penetrating your bones. Scattered pieces of brick and stone have been
discarded here in the dump. Where once a steady stream of horse-drawn cart
would carry the refuse of tarsis to this forsaken landfill, nothing stirs.
There is little here that is still useful, but the ancient bones of what
you can assume were vagrants lie amidst the trash, with the hopes of their
once peaceful lives covered with filth.

Before the Library
Two large wooden double doors in the southern wall once opened to
scholars seeking the knowledge and wisdom that was housed within the Great
Tarsis Library. Now only a single, beaten door remains, barely hanging from
its rusted hinges, threatening to fall and shatter itself on the stone
floor. The wall to the north is a crumbling testament to the power of time
and neglect: what was once relied upon to protect the city from invaders is
little more than a mound of stones that a small child could surmount.

The Tarsis Dump
A forsaken desert surrounds you, swallows you whole with its forceful
gales that hurl grains of sand deep into your skin. It is as if the wind is
penetrating your bones. Scattered pieces of brick and stone have been
discarded here in the dump. Where once a steady stream of horse-drawn cart
would carry the refuse of tarsis to this forsaken landfill, nothing stirs.
There is little here that is still useful, but the ancient bones of what
you can assume were vagrants lie amidst the trash, with the hopes of their
once peaceful lives covered with filth.

221H 114V 1807952X 6C Exits:NE> l
The Tarsis Dump
A forsaken desert surrounds you, swallows you whole with its forceful
gales that hurl grains of sand deep into your skin. It is as if the wind is
penetrating your bones. Scattered pieces of brick and stone have been
discarded here in the dump. Where once a steady stream of horse-drawn cart
would carry the refuse of tarsis to this forsaken landfill, nothing stirs.
There is little here that is still useful, but the ancient bones of what
you can assume were vagrants lie amidst the trash, with the hopes of their
once peaceful lives covered with filth.
A decaying vine rests on the ground.

. . . has a tough exterior.

A Shattered Gate
The southern gates of Tarsis were once heavily fortified, reinforced
steel, unlike their wooden counterparts at the north and east gates. These
gates were made specifically to keep something out, and to make sure that
it stayed out, especially since Icewall was to the south of this city
before the Gods took it away. The heavy fortifications and magical
enchantments on this gate are probably the only reason the gates still rest
on their massive hinges, although those hinges have long since rusted
solid.

North Gate
The northern gate of Tarsis once stood as an inpenetrable boundary to
would-be attackers from the Plains of Dust. Guards would patrol this area
and often and protected the cities inhabitants from the nomads and common
criminals that dwelled within the Plains. Now the shattered gate stands as
an eternal testament to their failure: the gate itself has long been torn
out of its frame and shattered onto the stone road of the city.

Before the Library
Two large wooden double doors in the southern wall once opened to
scholars seeking the knowledge and wisdom that was housed within the Great
Tarsis Library. Now only a single, beaten door remains, barely hanging from
its rusted hinges, threatening to fall and shatter itself on the stone
floor. The wall to the north is a crumbling testament to the power of time
and neglect: what was once relied upon to protect the city from invaders is
little more than a mound of stones that a small child could surmount.
